## Main strategic conclusion

I would **not** spend the next push primarily trying to prove \(\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})\) or \(\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}\). Those are hard global/arithmetic estimates, but even if they succeed, they do not close anything unless the \(Y12/K9\) channel is genuinely forbidden.

The highest-leverage attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Certify or kill }[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\ne0
\text{ in }
\mathcal Q_{9,Y12}^{\mathrm{forb},\alpha}.
}
\]

That is the best angle because it is the smallest finite-algebraic “switch” in the architecture. If it fails, the current downstream route is dead regardless of Gate–1. If it passes, then the remaining global estimates have a precise target.

## One issue I noticed in the draft

There is a subtle but important circularity risk in the finite/O2/O3 block.

The draft correctly says determinant survival should be proved **before capped extraction**, under a bounded-degree pre-extraction Stack weight. The handover also flags this as a required cleanup: finite/O2/O3 should use a pre-extraction bounded-degree weight, not the capped \(F_{\wall}^{\forb}\), for determinant survival. 

But the current `hyp:weighted-exterior-pivot-anti-trough-23` and `def:full-determinant-survival-stack-weight` still phrase \(d\nu\) using

\[
d\nu = F_1F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N\,d\rho.
\]

That is dangerous: \(F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}\) depends on the forbidden wall, which belongs **after** determinant survival and extraction. I would split this into two measures before launching agents:

\[
d\nu_{\mathrm{bd}}
=
F_1 N_{\mathrm{bd}}\,d\rho
\]

for bounded-degree determinant survival, and

\[
d\nu_{\mathrm{cap}}
=
F_1F_{23}F_{\mathrm{wall}}^{\mathrm{forb}}N\,d\rho
\]

for post-survival extraction / atomic contradiction.

This is not cosmetic. It is a non-circularity condition.

I would now give the agents **parallel kill-switch audits**, not broad proof-search prompts.

### Agent 1 — \(Y12\)-signature quotient kill-switch

Target:

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\ne0
\quad
\text{in}
\quad
\mathcal Q_{9,Y12}^{\mathrm{forb},\alpha}.

Tasks:

```text
You are Agent 1.

Audit the primitive Y12 forbidden quotient.

Work entirely at the finite algebraic/signature level. Do not attempt Gate--1,
O2/O3, or global estimates.

Define the finite projection

  Pi_{Sigma(Y12)}

and compute/test whether

  Pi_{Sigma(Y12)} T_{tr->sing}[C_{Y12}]

lies outside

  Pi_{Sigma(Y12)}(
    T_par^{(alpha)} + T_7 + T_<7 + II_{arith,9}
  ).

Return exactly one of:

  PROVED
  FINITE AUDIT
  NO-GO

If PROVED, give the finite basis, quotient matrix, and nonzero coordinate.

If FINITE AUDIT, give the exact matrix/rank computation still needed.

If NO-GO, identify which tangent/source-curvature subspace absorbs Y12.
```

### Agent 2 — actual-source tangent and \(\alpha\)-admission audit

Target: decide whether \(\alpha\), \(E_2\), or actual second curvature already spans the primitive \(Y12\) direction.

```text
You are Agent 2.

Audit whether the primitive Y12 channel is genuinely forbidden after actual
source tangents are admitted.

Check:

  Pi_{Sigma(Y12)} partial_alpha u,
  Pi_{Sigma(Y12)} partial_alpha^2 u,
  Pi_{Sigma(Y12)} II_{arith,9},
  Pi_{Sigma(Y12)} E_2.

Separate alpha used as proof-thickening from alpha admitted as an actual-source
parameter.

Classify E_2^Y as:

  absent/small,
  fixed/coherent graph,
  finite coherent amplitude,
  locally free tangent.

Return PROVED / FINITE AUDIT / NO-GO.

NO-GO means actual-source tangents or E_2 already contain the primitive Y12
normal direction.
```

### Agent 3 — \(R_{\sing}\) and \(\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{Y12}\)

Target: turn “forbidden” into an upper bound for actual rows.

```text
You are Agent 3.

Construct or kill the singular retained space R_sing for the Y12 channel.

Do not use a Taylor-complete retained space. It must be actual-source
EF-coherent and must not retain the D4 live carrier.

Prove or reduce both conditions:

  T_{tr->sing} J_tr(F_X) in R_sing,

and

  sum_p |Pi_{Sigma(Y12)} T_{tr->sing,p} J_{tr,p}(R_X)|^2
    <= Q^{-B} mu(C).

Here

  q''_can = F_X + R_X,
  F_X = B_2 + P_{2,<=X} + D_{2,<=X}.

Return PROVED / FINITE AUDIT / NO-GO.

Failure routes:
  R_sing too large,
  actual rows not retained,
  transition norm too large,
  Y12 residual completion unavailable.
```

### Agent 4 — non-circular extraction and measure split

Target: fix the bounded-degree/capped-measure issue.

```text
You are Agent 4.

Audit extraction non-circularity.

Separate the determinant-survival measure

  dnu_bd

from the post-extraction capped measure

  dnu_cap.

Finite/O2/O3 determinant survival must be proved under bounded-degree
pre-extraction weight, before introducing F_wall^forb.

Then prove/reduce a Lambda-compatible extraction theorem from:

  Agg L2,
  O2/O3 under dnu_bd,
  forbidden-wall visibility,

to a polynomial-mass capped set where all three survive.

Return PROVED / FINITE AUDIT / NO-GO.

If FINITE AUDIT, give the exact two measures and the allowed order of caps.
```

### Agent 5 — moving \(Y12\)-wall anti-concentration

Target: prevent the extracted measure from concentrating on the moving forbidden-wall kernel.

```text
You are Agent 5.

Assume the Y12 channel gives a moving linear form

  ell_p(Gamma) = a_p Gamma_G + b_p Gamma_{G,2},

with |b_p| >= Q^{-A} on coefficient-good packets.

Prove or reduce

  int |ell_p(Gamma)|^2 dnu
    >= Q^{-A} int (|Gamma_G|^2 + |Gamma_{G,2}|^2) dnu.

Do not use generic row energy. This must be anti-concentration for the actual
post-Gate/O2/O3 measure.

Return PROVED / FINITE AUDIT / NO-GO.

Failure means the measure can sit on the moving kernel of the forbidden wall.
```

### Agent 6 — arithmetic modules only after the forbidden channel is coherent

Target: keep Gate–1 and O2/O3 focused, but subordinate to the forbidden-channel test.

```text
You are Agent 6.

Audit the two global arithmetic inputs, but only in the form needed by the
Y12 forbidden-channel route.

Part A: Agg L2(q''_can)

Prove/reduce:

  ||q''_can||_{L2(W_branch)}^2
    >= Q^{-A} ||q''_can||_{L2(W_ref)}^2,

and

    >= Q^{-A} sum rho_b(m).

Use the finite truncation

  F_X = B_2 + P_{2,<=X} + D_{2,<=X}

and explicitly keep B_2 in the source.

Part B: Graph/O2O3_23

Prove/reduce the R^C-normalized graph obstruction

  dist(1/m_can, C_R[x]) >= Q^{-A}

and full determinant survival under bounded-degree pre-extraction weight.

Return PROVED / FINITE AUDIT / NO-GO.

Do not treat pure branch determinant mass as full scalar O2/O3.
```

## My recommendation

The next push should be framed as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the }Y12\text{ singular-discard channel actually be forbidden?}
}
\]

Everything else is secondary until that is answered. If \(Y12\) survives the quotient/tangent/\(E_2\) audits, then the proof has a concrete forbidden normal channel. If it does not, the current \(K9/Y12\) path should be demoted immediately, and the next search should move to either the \(C_7\) channel, a higher-order signature, or a different \(\Lambda\).

## Complete dependency map

The proof spine decomposes as follows.

### 1. Canonical source layer

Everything must be stated for

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

A result for \(P_2\)-only, \(B_2\)-only, zero-side proxies, ordinary packet rows, or singular sine diagnostics is not sufficient unless it transfers to scalar \(L^2(q''_{\can})\).

### 2. Active Gate–1 layer

The live Gate–1 object is:

\[
\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can}):
\qquad
\int |q''_{\can}(t)|^2 W_{\branch}(t)\,dt
\ge
Q^{-A}\mathcal N_{\can}(W_{\branch}).
\]

This splits into:

\[
\mathrm{Coverage}_{q''}
+
\mathrm{MeanSq}_{q''_{\can}}
+
\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{L^2}.
\]

The old finite-row O1/O2/O3 route should not be reopened as the primary route. Its dimension defect is real: \(O(R)\) observed rows are too few for pointwise exclusion across exponentially many zero candidates unless one assumes a counter-random projection theorem.

### 3. Finite/O2O3 layer

This is now an analytic \(R^C\)-conditioned Riesz/exterior-pivot problem, not Gate–2.

The key module is:

\[
A_{\le X,m}
\quad\text{built from}\quad
F_X=B_2+P_{2,\le X}+D_{2,\le X},
\]

with graph space

\[
\mathbf C\cdot1+m_{\can}\mathbf C_R[x]
=
m_{\can}\left(\mathbf C\cdot(1/m_{\can})+\mathbf C_R[x]\right).
\]

The real burden is not the pure graph estimate alone. It is full determinant survival under a smooth bounded-degree pre-extraction Stack weight. Capped extraction must come after this, not before.

### 4. Local rank-two/D4 layer

The row-normal D4 block is structurally organized now. The selector is

\[
r_Y
=
\operatorname{rank}
\left(
\Pi_{\mathbf C^2/B_Y}M_{\D4}^{\tri}
\right),
\qquad
M_{\D4}^{\tri}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
\beta_9^{\tri}&\alpha_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

If \(B_Y=0\) and \(c_7\alpha_9\neq0\), D4 supplies

\[
H
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
\beta_9^{\tri}\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
\asymp
H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

But this is **visibility**, not contradiction.

### 5. Forbidden-channel layer

This is the decisive layer. The current best candidate is the \(Y12/K9\) singular-discard channel:

\[
\Lambda_{\tr,\sing,p}
=
(I-P_{\sing,p})T_{\tr\to\sing,p}P_{\tr,p}.
\]

The \(Y12\)-normal route needs:

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\neq0
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathcal Q_{9,Y12}^{\forb,\alpha},
\]

plus:

\[
\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{Y12},
\qquad
\mathrm{LowerOrderTangentObservability}_{K9},
\qquad
\mathrm{MovingWallAntiConcentration}_{Y12},
\qquad
\mathrm{TubularNormality}_{\sing}.
\]

If this \(Y12\) class is absorbed by actual-source tangents, \(\alpha\)-tangents, \(E_2^Y\), lower connection effects, or \(\mathcal{II}_{\arith,9}\), then the current finite-D4 contradiction path dies even if D4 remains locally visible.

## Best strategic plan

I would not make the next push a general “prove Gate–1” campaign. That is too broad. I would run a **three-front closure/falsification campaign**.

### Front A — \(Y12\) finite kill-switch

This is the highest-leverage test.

Prove or kill:

\[
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\neq0
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathcal Q_{9,Y12}^{\forb,\alpha}.
\]

This should be treated as a finite quotient/tangent audit, not a global zeta estimate. If it fails, the current \(K9/Y12\) normal-D4 route should be demoted immediately.

The audit must include:

\[
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
\left(
\mathcal T_{\par}^{(\alpha)}
+
\mathcal T_7
+
\mathcal T_{<7}
+
\mathcal{II}_{\arith,9}
\right),
\]

and must classify \(E_2^Y\) as absent/small, fixed graph, finite coherent amplitude, or locally free tangent.

### Front B — non-circular extraction and finite/O2O3

This is the next structural risk. The draft must keep these two measures separate:

\[
d\nu_{\bd}
=
\text{smooth bounded-degree pre-extraction Stack measure},
\]

used for determinant survival, and

\[
d\nu_{\cap}
=
F_1F_{23}F_{\wall}^{\forb}N\,d\rho,
\]

used only after determinant survival and forbidden-wall visibility are available.

If determinant survival uses the forbidden-wall cap too early, the argument becomes circular.

### Front C — aggregate \(L^2(q''_{\can})\)

This is the main upstream analytic input, but it should be attacked only in the active aggregate form:

\[
\|q''_{\can}\|_{L^2(W_{\branch})}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\|q''_{\can}\|_{L^2(W_{\ref})}^2,
\]

and

\[
\|q''_{\can}\|_{L^2(W_{\ref})}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\sum_{b,m}\rho_b(m).
\]

The finite-row O1/O2/O3 bad-zero route should stay archived unless someone proves the counter-random projection theorem explicitly.

## Recommended parallel agent split

I would assign the six agents as follows, all independently runnable.

**Agent 1 — \(Y12\)-signature quotient.**  
Compute/test whether \([\mathsf C_{Y12}]\neq0\) in \(\mathcal Q_{9,Y12}^{\forb,\alpha}\). Return `PROVED`, `FINITE AUDIT`, or `NO-GO`.

**Agent 2 — actual-source tangent audit.**  
Check whether \(\alpha\)-tangents, \(E_2^Y\), \(\mathcal{II}_{\arith,9}\), or lower connection effects absorb the primitive \(Y12\) direction.

**Agent 3 — singular retained space and \(\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{Y12}\).**  
Define \(R_{\sing}\) so actual rows are retained but the D4 \(Y12\) carrier is discarded. Rule out Taylor-complete/functorial retained spaces.

**Agent 4 — finite/O2O3 non-circularity.**  
Separate smooth determinant-survival measure from capped extraction measure. Prove/reduce full determinant survival before any \(F_{\wall}^{\forb}\) cap.

**Agent 5 — aggregate \(L^2(q''_{\can})\).**  
Attack coverage, reference mean-square, and finite AFE completion for the full canonical source. No finite-row Gate–1 substitutions.

**Agent 6 — moving-wall/extraction compatibility.**  
Prove or reduce \(\Lambda\)-compatible extraction and moving \(Y12\)-wall anti-concentration under the post-Gate/O2O3 measure.

## Coordinator priority

The synthesis should answer these questions, in this order conceptually, though the agents can work in parallel:

\[
\boxed{
1.\ \text{Does the \(Y12\)-normal forbidden class survive?}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
2.\ \text{Can actual rows be made small in the discarded singular direction?}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
3.\ \text{Can determinant survival and extraction be made non-circular?}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
4.\ \text{Can aggregate \(L^2(q''_{\can})\) be proved for the actual branch weights?}
}
\]

If the answer to 1 is no, the current \(K9/Y12\) path dies. If 1 is yes but 2 fails, singular-discard is not forbidden. If 1 and 2 pass but 3 fails, extraction is circular. If 1–3 pass, then the upstream \(L^2\) theorem becomes the main remaining analytic problem.

That is the cleanest strategy I see from the current draft.

# Shared background for all agents

```text
We are working on a conditional RH obstruction architecture, not a completed proof. Do not claim RH is proved.

The current live architecture is:

  Agg L2(q''_can)
  + Graph/O2O3_23
  + NormalD4_{K9,Y12}.

Current Gate--1:

  Gate--1 is aggregate scalar local L2 energy of the full canonical source

    q''_can = B_2 + P_2 + D_2 + E_2.

  For a branch b,

    F_{b,m}(x) = lambda_b^3 q''_can(m + lambda_b x),

    E_{1,b}^{L2}(m) = int_{I_b} |F_{b,m}(x)|^2 w_b(x) dx.

  The aggregate input is

    int |q''_can(t)|^2 W_branch(t) dt
      >= Q^{-A} N_can(W_branch).

Old O1/O2/O3, S1/T1, transition jets, singular sine diagnostics, and branch-specific finite rows are proof tools or historical alternate routes only. Do not reintroduce them as the active Gate--1 definition.

Current O2/O3:

  O2/O3 is separate from Gate--2. It is a finite analytic nondegeneracy module using an R^C-conditioned Riesz basis.

  The finite augmented space is

    C*1 + m_can C_R[x]
      =
    m_can( C*(1/m_can) + C_R[x] ).

  The harmonic exterior quantity is

    H_23(A) = |det A|^2 / sum_{i,j} |Cof_{ij}(A)|^2,

  and for n=R+2,

    (1/n) sigma_min(A)^2 <= H_23(A) <= sigma_min(A)^2.

  Need R^C-normalization, not merely Q^C-normalization.

  Pure branch determinant lower bounds are not enough. Need full determinant survival in the full canonical matrix.

Current D4/rank-two rules:

  D4 supplies only the plain wall

    H(Gamma_G, Gamma_{G,2}).

  Do not introduce a derivative wall H(Gamma_G, D Gamma_G, D^2 Gamma_G, Gamma_{G,2}) unless proving a separate derivative-D4-channel theorem.

  Use row-normal coefficients only:

    kappa = omega_Y(e_7),
    ell_9^Y = omega_Y - kappa ell_7,
    beta_9^tri = beta_9 - kappa c_7.

  The row-normal D4 matrix is

    M_D4^tri =
      [[c_7, 0],
       [beta_9^tri, alpha_9]].

  The rank selector is

    r_Y = rank( Pi_{C^2/B_Y} M_D4^tri ).

  If B_Y=0, then r_Y=2 iff c_7 alpha_9 != 0.

Current forbidden-channel target:

  D4 local carrier visibility is not a contradiction theorem.

  A contradiction requires a forbidden channel Lambda with

    |Lambda V_glob|^2 <= Q^{-B} mu(C)

  and

    rank(Lambda E_car L_clean) >= 1

  on the live D4 plane.

  The current preferred channel is the transition--singular / K9,Y12 normal channel, not generic row energy.

Current NormalD4_{K9,Y12} target:

  The minimal downstream D4 contradiction channel is the primitive Y12-signature quotient, not full K9 unless full K9 is actually needed.

  Need

    [C_{Y12}] != 0 in Q_{9,Y12}^{forb,alpha},

  where the quotient removes actual-source tangents, T_7, T_<7, and II_{arith,9}.

  Also need:

    EFCompletion_Y12,
    lower-order tangent observability for K9,
    moving Y12-wall anti-concentration,
    tubular normality of the singular retained space,
    singular-discard upper.

Alpha caveat:

  Alpha twisting is conditional. Do not admit alpha as an actual-source tangent unless AlphaD4Compatibility is proved. If partial_alpha u or partial_alpha^2 u has primitive Y12-signature, it may kill the Y12-normal quotient.

Dead/no-go routes:

  Optimized Xi_N is rank-zero on current finite D4 order 7/9.
  Low-N Xi is diagnostic unless a new low-order forbidden identity is proved.
  One-parameter row mobility is not a forbidden identity.
  Functorial carrier lifts are rank-zero if they retain the D4 live plane.
  Scalar I-coordinate D4 and derivative-wall D4 remain quarantined.
  Full K9-or-bust is stale unless Y12 fails.

Each agent must return exactly one of:

  PROVED
  FINITE AUDIT
  NO-GO

and give exact definitions, finite spaces, matrices, rank conditions, and failure routing. Avoid broad strategy. Do math.
```

# Agent 1 — \(\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})\)

```text
You are Agent 1.

Target:
  Close or finitely reduce Agg L2(q''_can).

Active Gate--1 is scalar local L2 energy of

  q''_can = B_2 + P_2 + D_2 + E_2,

not finite-row O1/O2/O3, S1/T1, transition jets, singular sine moments, or branch diagnostics.

Tasks:

1. State the exact branch-complete aggregate theorem.

   Define

     F_{b,m}(x) = lambda_b^3 q''_can(m + lambda_b x),

     E_{1,b}^{L2}(m) = int_{I_b} |F_{b,m}(x)|^2 w_b(x) dx,

   and

     W_branch(t)
       =
     sum_b sum_{m in C_b}
       rho_b(m) lambda_b^5
       w_b((t-m)/lambda_b).

   Prove or finitely reduce

     int |q''_can(t)|^2 W_branch(t) dt
       >= Q^{-A} N_can(W_branch).

2. Define N_can(W_branch) precisely.

   Decide whether N_can is:
     diagonal finite AFE mass,
     continuous reference source energy,
     branch-local packet mass,
     or another canonical norm.

   Then prove/reduce

     N_can(W_branch) >= Q^{-A} sum_b sum_m rho_b(m).

3. Split the proof into:

   Coverage_{q''}:
     W_branch samples the |q''_can|^2 energy measure.

   MeanSq_{q''_can}:
     full canonical source has nontrivial weighted mean square.

   EFCompletion_L2:
     q''_can = F_X + R_X,
     F_X = B_2 + P_{2,<=X} + D_{2,<=X},

     with

     ||R_X||_{L2(W_branch)}^2 + ||R_X||_{L2(W_ref)}^2
       <= Q^{-B} ||F_X||_{L2(W_ref)}^2.

4. Audit B_2.

   B_2 is part of the canonical source. Do not treat it as perturbative unless you prove weighted L2 perturbativity or incorporate it into F_X.

5. Test finite AFE anti-lock:

     ||B_2 + P_{2,<=X} + D_{2,<=X}||_{L2(W_branch)}^2
       >= Q^{-A}
     ||B_2 + P_{2,<=X} + D_{2,<=X}||_{L2(W_ref)}^2.

6. Identify exact failure routing:

   branch holes,
   finite AFE anti-lock failure,
   residual completion failure,
   reference mean-square collapse,
   gamma/background dominance/cancellation,
   true local source flatness.

Deliverable:
  PROVED / FINITE AUDIT / NO-GO.

If FINITE AUDIT:
  give the exact weights, truncation scale, residual estimate, and source nonflatness theorem still needed.
```

# Agent 2 — \(\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}\)

```text
You are Agent 2.

Target:
  Close or finitely reduce Graph/O2O3_23.

O2/O3 is separate from Gate--2. It is an analytic finite-dimensional nondegeneracy theorem in an R^C-conditioned Riesz basis.

Tasks:

1. Define the finite augmented matrix

     A_{<=X,m}

   built from

     F_X = B_2 + P_{2,<=X} + D_{2,<=X}

   and augmented column space

     C*1 + m_can C_R[x].

2. Prove/reduce R^C-normalization:

     ||A_{<=X,m}||_op <= R^C

   in the chosen analytic Riesz basis.

   A Q^C bound is not enough, because determinant-to-sigma_min conversion loses Q^{O(R)}.

3. Prove/reduce the graph model:

     C*1 + m_can C_R[x]
       =
     m_can( C*(1/m_can) + C_R[x] ).

   Need

     dist_Riesz(1/m_can, C_R[x]) >= Q^{-A}.

4. Prove/reduce the canonical quadratic multiplier theorem:

     m_can,+ (x) = kappa (x-z0)^2 u(x),

   with polynomial bounds on kappa, u, 1/u, and divided differences through order R+1.

   Derive

     dist(1/m_can,+, C_R[x]) >= Q^{-A}.

5. Prove/reduce full determinant survival.

   Pure branch graph mass is not scalar O2/O3. Need full determinant survival:

     int |D_full|^2 dnu
       >= Q^{-A}
     int |D_dom|^2 dnu.

   Specify the measure dnu. It must be pre-extraction / bounded-degree if determinant survival is being proved before capped extraction.

6. Audit alpha use.

   If alpha-twist is invoked, prove AlphaAdmissibility+:
     zero persistence,
     badness persistence,
     twist speed,
     Stack uniformity,
     D4 compatibility.

   If AlphaD4Compatibility fails, alpha cannot be admitted as an actual-source tangent.

7. State whether O2/O3 is proved by:
     R^C graph non-polynomiality alone,
     graph plus full determinant survival,
     alpha-averaged determinant survival,
     or a named remaining arithmetic input.

Deliverable:
  PROVED / FINITE AUDIT / NO-GO.

If FINITE AUDIT:
  give the exact matrix A, basis normalization, graph-distance theorem, full determinant survival statement, and alpha caveats.

Failure routing:
  Riesz normalization fails,
  1/m_can is too polynomial,
  pure graph does not survive in full determinant,
  alpha is not admissible,
  capped extraction was applied too early.
```

## Assistant (2026-04-28 20:13:06)

_Thought for 11s_

Read the agent responses. The round is productive: all agents return **FINITE AUDIT**, but the architecture is now much more finite and checkable. The current route is not “vague upstream arithmetic + vague D4 contradiction” anymore. It has become a stack of explicit Gram/Schur/projection/covariance tests. 

# Coordinator synthesis

The live stack is now best written as:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})
+
\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}
+
\mathrm{Labelled/Discarded}\ Y12\text{-Normal D4}
+
\mathrm{AtomicY12Contradiction}.
}
\]

The main updates are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate--1 is finite-auditable through packet-core micro-covering.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{O2/O3 is finite-auditable through genuine-pole graph distance plus thickened Schur survival.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Y12 survival should use labelled transition, not raw }ad+bc.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The contradiction layer now reduces to three exact quotient tests.}
}
\]

## 1. Agent 1 — \(\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})\)

Agent 1 has reduced aggregate Gate–1 to a concrete finite sampling problem.

The active theorem remains:

\[
\int |q''_{\can}(t)|^2 W_{\branch}(t)\,dt
\ge
Q^{-A}\mathcal N_{\can}(W_{\branch}),
\]

with

\[
\mathcal N_{\can}(W_{\branch})
=
\int |q''_{\can}(t)|^2 W_{\ref}(t)\,dt.
\]

The finite reduction is:

\[
F_X=B_2+P_{2,\le X}+D_{2,\le X},
\qquad
R_X=q''_{\can}-F_X,
\qquad
X=e^{Q/2}.
\]

Gate–1 follows from:

\[
|F_X|_{L^2(W_{\branch})}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}|F_X|_{L^2(W_{\ref})}^2,
\]

\[
|F_X|_{L^2(W_{\ref})}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\sum_p\rho_p,
\]

and

\[
|R_X|_{L^2(W_{\branch})}^2+
|R_X|_{L^2(W_{\ref})}^2
\le
Q^{-B}|F_X|_{L^2(W_{\ref})}^2.
\]

The important new sharpening is that finite anti-lock is reduced to packet-core micro-covering. Define packet cores \(K_p\), and set

\[
K=\bigcup_p K_p.
\]

The key geometric certificate is:

\[
\Gamma_*
=
\inf_{|J|=C\log Q/Q}
\frac{|J\cap K|}{|J|}
\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and

\[
\Delta_*
=
\inf_{t\in K}
\frac{W_{\branch}(t)}{W_{\ref}(t)}
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If these hold, then Logvinenko–Sereda/Nazarov sampling gives the finite anti-lock estimate with polynomial loss.

So Agent 1’s final missing input is now very precise:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-core micro-covering at scale } \log Q/Q,
}
\]

or, if that fails,

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual-source anti-trough on uncovered holes.}
}
\]

This is a strong cleanup. The old “finite-row projection” issue is gone from the active Gate–1 definition.

## 2. Agent 2 — \(\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}\)

Agent 2 sharpened O2/O3 into four finite inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{RieszNorm}_{23}
+
\mathrm{GenuinePole}_R
+
\mathrm{SectorialDivDiff}_R
+
\mathrm{ThickenedSchur}_{23}.
}
\]

The graph step needs more than a quadratic factorization

\[
m_{\can,+}(x)=\kappa(x-z_0)^2u(x).
\]

It needs a **genuine non-cancelled pole** for \(1/m_{\can,+}\). Otherwise \(u\) could cancel the pole and make \(1/m_{\can,+}\) polynomial-like.

The correct graph-distance certificate is a sectorial divided-difference test:

\[
\operatorname{dist}_{\mathcal R_R}
(1/m_{\can,+},\mathbf C_R[x])
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The pure graph determinant still does not close scalar O2/O3. Need full determinant survival:

\[
\int |D_{\full}|^2\,d\nu_{\pre}
\ge
Q^{-A}
\int |D_{\dom}|^2\,d\nu_{\pre}.
\]

Agent 2 first tried valuation separation, but corrected it: valuation alone fails under non-neutral Stack weights. The Stack weight can bridge branch-charge gaps.

The correct determinant survival object is a **thickened-frequency Schur complement**. After Fejér–Riesz factorization of the bounded-degree Stack weight,

\[
\Omega_{\stk}=|P_{\stk}|^2,
\]

the survival condition becomes:

\[
\operatorname{dist}_{L^2(d\rho)}
\left(
P_{\stk}D_0,\,
P_{\stk}\operatorname{span}\{D_1,\dots,D_{d_0}\}
\right)^2
\ge
Q^{-A}|P_{\stk}D_0|^2.
\]

Equivalently, compute the Schur complement after Stack-thickening:

\[
G_{00}-G_{0S}G_{SS}^{\dagger}G_{S0}
\ge Q^{-A}G_{00}.
\]

So Agent 2’s remaining audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{compute or prove the thickened-frequency Schur lower bound.}
}
\]

This is much sharper than “prove O2/O3.”

## 3. Agent 3 — labelled \(Y12\) transition replaces raw \(ad+bc\)

Agent 3’s main result is important.

The earlier raw transition obstruction

\[
ad+bc=0
\]

is **not intrinsic**. It appears only when the transition recomputes the source Hessian in raw coordinates.

The better route is labelled transition:

\[
\widetilde T_{\tr\to\sing}^{\lab},
\]

which transports the already-formed labelled primitive carrier

\[
\Sigma(Y12)
=
(2,D^2N_0,\text{mixed }12,\text{same point},w=1,o=9).
\]

Then the target becomes:

\[
\Pi_Y\operatorname{Real}_{\sing}
\widetilde T_{\tr\to\sing}^{\lab}
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
=
\gamma_Ys_Y^{\sing}
+
\Pi_YR_{\lab}.
\]

So the finite survival test is no longer \(ad+bc\neq0\). It is:

\[
|\gamma_Y|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

\[
\Pi_YR_{\lab}
\text{ is not locally free},
\]

and

\[
s_Y^{\sing}
\notin
\Pi_Y
\left(
\mathcal N_{\exact}
+
T_{\par}^{(\alpha)}
+
T_7+
T_{<7}
+
\mathcal{II}_{\arith,9}^{Y}
+
T_{E_2}^{\free}
+
R_{\lab}^{\free}
\right).
\]

This is a real improvement. It demotes \(ad+bc\) to a raw-realization fallback/no-go, not the primary \(Y12\) criterion.

The labelled route gives the rank-one D4 wall:

\[
H\gamma_Y^{\eff}
\left(
(\beta_9^{\tri}-\rho_Yc_7)\Gamma_G
+
\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\right),
\]

with rank at least one if

\[
|\gamma_Y^{\eff}\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

So Agent 3’s finite audit is now:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{LabelPreserve}_{Y12}
+
\mathrm{RealizationConsistency}_{Y12}
+
\mathrm{NoFree}R_{\lab}^Y
+
\mathrm{NoFree}E_2^Y
+
|\gamma_Y|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

## 4. Agent 4 — EF completion and retained-space sandwich

Agent 4 has reduced the singular retained/discarded layer to exact finite linear algebra.

The key object is the retained singular space:

\[
R_{\sing,p}\subset H_{\sing,p}^{\le 9},
\]

with projection \(P_p\). The preferred \(Y12\) carrier vector is:

\[
d_{Y,p}
=
T_{\tr\to\sing,p}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]^{\tr}.
\]

The \(Y12\)-normal route survives iff:

\[
r_{Y,p}:=(I-P_p)d_{Y,p}\neq0,
\]

quantitatively:

\[
|r_{Y,p}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

The exact finite test is a Schur complement. If \(A_p\) spans the retained space,

\[
G_p=A_p^*A_p,
\qquad
b_{Y,p}=A_p^*d_{Y,p},
\qquad
q_{Y,p}=d_{Y,p}^*d_{Y,p},
\]

then

\[
|r_{Y,p}|^2
=
q_{Y,p}-b_{Y,p}^*G_p^\dagger b_{Y,p}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\Delta_p(d_{Y,p})
=
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
G_p&A_p^*d_{Y,p}\\
d_{Y,p}^*A_p&d_{Y,p}^*d_{Y,p}
\end{pmatrix}
>0.
\]

The major guardrail is the retained-space sandwich:

\[
\boxed{
\text{retain actual EF-coherent rows, but do not retain }d_{Y,p}.
}
\]

Larger retained spaces make the forbidden upper easier but D4 visibility harder. The exact danger is:

\[
d_{Y,p}\in R_{\sing,p}.
\]

Agent 4 also sharply separates:

\[
\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{L^2},
\qquad
\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{K9},
\qquad
\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{Y12},
\qquad
\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{\discard}.
\]

The important no-go is:

\[
\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{L^2}
\not\Rightarrow
\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{K9/Y12/\discard}
\]

without analytic sampling. Real-line \(L^2\) alone cannot control order-nine jets.

So Agent 4’s remaining inputs are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{analytic discard completion for }R_X,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|r_{Y,p}|^2
=
q_{Y,p}-b_{Y,p}^*G_p^\dagger b_{Y,p}
\ge Q^{-C},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{tubular normality of the actual-source singular manifold.}
}
\]

## 5. Agent 5 — extraction compressed to PSD covariance tests

Agent 5 has compressed extraction into finite positive semidefinite matrices.

For each packet define:

\[
w_p
=
\rho_p\frac{E_{1,p}H_p}{N_p},
\]

where \(E_{1,p}\) is finite scalar \(L^2\) Gate–1 energy and

\[
H_p=\mathcal H_{23}(A_p).
\]

Define the pre-wall covariance:

\[
B_C
=
\sum_{p\in C}
w_p\Gamma_p\Gamma_p^*
\in \mathrm{Herm}_2^+.
\]

Then pre-wall coexistence is exactly:

\[
\operatorname{tr}B_C
\ge Q^{-A}\mu(C).
\]

This replaces vague “joint overlap.”

The \(Y12\)-wall mass is:

\[
\sum_{p\in C}w_p|M_p\Gamma_p|^2,
\]

where

\[
M_p
=
\Lambda^Y_pE^{\tr}_{\car,p}L^{\tr}_{\clean,p}
\big|_{\langle [C_7],[C_{Y12}]\rangle}.
\]

Rank-zero exclusion is:

\[
\operatorname{tr}B_0
\le Q^{-A}\operatorname{tr}B_C.
\]

Rank two is handled by:

\[
\sigma_{\min}(M_p)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Rank one reduces to angular caps. For each cap \(j\), define:

\[
B_j
=
\sum_{p\in C_j}
w_p\Gamma_p\Gamma_p^*.
\]

Then moving-wall anti-concentration is exactly the \(2\times2\) PSD test:

\[
v_j^*B_jv_j
\ge
Q^{-A}\operatorname{tr}B_j.
\]

This is the best extraction formulation so far.

Agent 5’s exact remaining finite audits are:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{tr}B_C\ge Q^{-A}\mu(C),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{tr}B_{\bad}\le Q^{-A}\operatorname{tr}B_C,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{tr}B_0\le Q^{-A}\operatorname{tr}B_C,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
v_j^*B_jv_j\ge Q^{-A}\operatorname{tr}B_j
\quad\text{for frozen rank-one caps.}
}
\]

This is a clean finite covariance audit.

## 6. Agent 6 — final contradiction reduced to three exact tests

Agent 6 now has the sharpest result of the round.

The contradiction layer reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{QuotientCompatibility}_{D4\to Y12}
+
\mathrm{PrimitiveCarrierSurvival}_{Y12}
+
\mathrm{QuotientEFCompletion}_{Y12}
+
\mathrm{MovingWallAntiConcentration}_{Y12}.
}
\]

The key insight is quotient factorization. Let

\[
\pi_p^{D4}:V_p\to \mathcal D_p=V_p/N_p^{D4}
\]

be the D4 quotient. The \(Y12\) observable

\[
\Lambda_{Y,p}
=
q_p\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
T_{\tr\to\sing,p}P_{\tr,p}
\]

can use the D4 theorem only if it factors through the same quotient:

\[
N_p^{D4}\subseteq \ker\Lambda_{Y,p}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\Lambda_{Y,p}
=
\widetilde\Lambda_{Y,p}\pi_p^{D4}.
\]

The exact finite matrix test is:

\[
q_p\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
T_{\tr\to\sing}
\mathcal N_p^{D4}
=0.
\]

Or with the killed-space matrix \(\mathcal K_p\):

\[
\operatorname{rank}
\left[
\mathcal K_p
\quad
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
T_{\tr\to\sing}
\mathcal N_p^{D4}
\right]
=
\operatorname{rank}\mathcal K_p.
\]

The primitive carrier survival test is:

\[
\operatorname{rank}
\left[
\mathcal K_p
\quad
Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}
\right]
>
\operatorname{rank}\mathcal K_p,
\]

where

\[
Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}
=
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
T_{\tr\to\sing}
[\mathsf C_{Y12}]^{\tr}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
r_{Y,p}
=
(I-P_{\mathcal K_p}^{\bd})Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}
\]

must satisfy:

\[
|r_{Y,p}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The Type-I upper becomes quotient EF completion:

\[
\sum_p
\left|
(I-P_{\mathcal K_p}^{\bd})
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
T_{\tr\to\sing}
J_{\tr,p}(R_X)
\right|^2
\le Q^{-B}\mu(\mathcal C).
\]

This is the cleanest final audit.

Agent 6’s key no-gos are:

\[
\boxed{
Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}\in\operatorname{im}\mathcal K_p
\Rightarrow
\text{primitive }Y12\text{ is killed.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}
T_{\tr\to\sing}\mathcal N_p^{D4}
\not\subseteq
\operatorname{im}\mathcal K_p
\Rightarrow
\text{D4 quotient incompatible with }Y12\text{ observable.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{quotient EF completion fails}
\Rightarrow
\text{no Type-I upper in the needed norm.}
}
\]

The proof architecture has become a sequence of finite Gram/Schur/covariance lower bounds.

# Recommended next agent round

I would now stop broad exploration. The next round should ask agents to attack the **exact finite tests**.

Suggested split:

1. **Agent 1:** prove/check packet-core micro-covering at scale \(\log Q/Q\), or formulate actual-source anti-trough on uncovered holes.

2. **Agent 2:** compute/prove \(\mathrm{ThickenedSchur}_{23}\) after Fejér–Riesz Stack thickening.

3. **Agent 3:** formalize labelled transition realization and compute \(\gamma_Y\), \(R_{\lab}\), and the labelled/raw consistency defect.

4. **Agent 4:** build \(\mathcal K_p\) explicitly and compute the Schur residual \(r_{Y,p}\).

5. **Agent 5:** compute the PSD matrices \(B_C,B_j\) and identify conditions under which \(v_j^*B_jv_j\) cannot be small.

6. **Agent 6:** prove quotient compatibility

\[

T_{\tr\to\sing}
\mathcal N_p^{D4}
\subseteq
\mathcal K_p
\]

and quotient EF completion in the exact same norm.

This round is highly useful. The architecture is still not proved, but it is no longer vague. The remaining live work is now finite and explicit:

because that kills the primitive \(Y12\)-normal route outright.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 20:14:38)

_Thought for 5s_

I read them again carefully. The main hidden connection is that all six threads are really the same proof pattern in different coordinate systems: pick a finite good subspace, quotient out nuisance directions, then prove that the remaining observable has a positive-semidefinite lower bound and a matching Type-I upper bound. 

The strongest cross-thread insights are these.

First, Agent 1, Agent 2, and Agent 5 are all doing the same thing at different levels of the stack. Agent 1’s packet-core micro-covering, Agent 2’s thickened Schur survival, and Agent 5’s covariance matrix \(B_C\) are all finite “mass survives after localization” statements. They differ only in the object being localized: scalar source energy for Gate–1, determinant mass for O2/O3, and D4-plane amplitude for the extraction layer. That means the proof architecture is converging toward one abstract lemma: “a weighted tensor/cofactor determinant cannot concentrate on a thin bad subset without violating a finite PSD lower bound.” 

Second, Agent 3 and Agent 6 are now tightly coupled. Agent 3’s labelled transition route replaces the raw \(ad+bc\) obstruction by a labelled carrier scalar \(\gamma_Y\), while Agent 6’s final contradiction requires exactly that the \(Y12\) observable factors through the same quotient as the D4 carrier. The hidden point is that labelled transition is not just a cleaner formulation; it is what makes the quotient compatibility test meaningful. Without labelled preservation, Agent 6’s \(Y12\) observable may not even descend from the D4 quotient, so the contradiction would be ill-posed rather than merely unproved. 

Third, Agent 4 and Agent 6 are actually the same sandwich lemma written in two languages. Agent 4 says the retained singular space must contain the actual EF-coherent source row \(S_p\) but not the \(Y12\) carrier \(d_{Y,p}\). Agent 6 says the killed space \(\mathcal K_p\) must contain the actual source nuisance directions but not the primitive \(Y12\) target \(Y^{\tar}_{Y,p}\). These are identical after taking the quotient viewpoint seriously. So the real invariant is not “retained space” or “forbidden quotient” separately, but the membership test
\[
Y^{\tar}_{Y,p}\in \mathcal K_p \quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad \text{route dies}.
\]
That is the cleanest no-go criterion in the whole round. 

Fourth, the extraction layer and the final contradiction layer are now one object in disguise. Agent 5’s covariance matrix \(B_j\) on a frozen angular cap and Agent 6’s moving-wall vector \(a_p\Gamma_G+b_p\Gamma_{G,2}\) are the same 2D geometry. The hidden connection is that the extraction theorem is not just a precursor; it is already the exact finite nonconcentration statement needed for the final forbidden upper. In other words, the wall anti-concentration is the lower-half of the contradiction, and the Type-I singular-discard upper is the upper-half. They meet through the same \(2\times2\) PSD matrix. 

Fifth, Agent 1 and Agent 2 share a surprisingly strong structural analogy. Agent 1’s “packet-core thickness at scale \(\log Q/Q\)” and Agent 2’s “Stack-thickened frequency Schur complement” are both density-vs-resolution statements. One asks whether the branch packets sample the canonical source densely enough to prevent anti-lock; the other asks whether the Stack-weighted frequency support leaves a nonzero determinant after quotienting nuisance directions. Both are really saying: does the bad set occupy enough thickness in the relevant finite resolution to kill polynomial lower bounds? That is why both agents ended up with finite Gram/Schur certificates rather than asymptotic estimates. 

Sixth, the round exposed one recurring structural no-go that now appears in three places: if the nuisance/tangent space becomes too large, the route collapses. In Agent 3, admitting \(\alpha\) or \(E_2^Y\) into the quotient can kill the labelled \(Y12\) carrier. In Agent 4, a carrier-complete retained space kills the D4 channel. In Agent 6, if the D4 nuisance quotient does not factor through the \(Y12\) observable, the contradiction cannot even be formulated in the same norm. So the shared discipline is: every enlargement of the retained/nuisance space must be tested against the survival of the primitive \(Y12\) vector. That is the deepest hidden coupling between the threads. 

Seventh, there is a useful consolidation opportunity: the paper is really proving one “finite survival theorem” in four manifestations. The manifestations are Gate–1 source survival, O2/O3 determinant survival, \(Y12\) labelled carrier survival, and D4 extraction survival. Each one has the same skeleton:
a finite observable,
a killed space,
a quotient or Schur complement,
and a polynomial lower bound. The whole project becomes much clearer if those are unified as a single survival meta-lemma with four instantiations. 

The most important hidden insight is probably this: the route is not looking for a large lower bound anywhere. It is looking for a lower bound that survives **the same quotient** used by the forbidden upper. That is why Agent 6’s quotient compatibility test is so central, and why Agent 3’s labelled transition matters so much. The proof only closes if the lower and upper are measured in exactly the same projected space. 

One concise way to summarize the whole round is:

\[
\text{good packets}
\;\to\;
\text{finite PSD mass}
\;\to\;
\text{quotient survival}
\;\to\;
\text{same-norm atomic upper}
\;\to\;
\text{contradiction}.
\]

That is the hidden common spine across all six threads.

## Assistant (2026-04-28 20:15:42)

_Thought for 4s_

Yes. The cleanest reformulation is to make the whole proof one **finite survival theorem** with four instantiations, instead of three partially overlapping subsystems. Right now the draft has the right ingredients, but they are still phrased as separate “Gate–1 / O2-O3 / Y12 / extraction / contradiction” modules. Those should be unified into one architecture:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite source survival}
\;\Rightarrow\;
\text{finite graph survival}
\;\Rightarrow\;
\text{quotient survival}
\;\Rightarrow\;
\text{atomic contradiction}.
}
\]

That is the common spine behind the six threads. 

## Unified architecture

### 1) Finite source layer
Start with the canonical source
\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]
The first theorem is not “Gate–1 in the old branch-row sense,” but a **source survival theorem**:

\[
\|q''_{\can}\|_{L^2(W_{\branch})}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}\|q''_{\can}\|_{L^2(W_{\ref})}^2.
\]

This is proved by finite sampling/thickness of packet cores at scale \(\log Q/Q\), plus EF completion. So the role of the source layer is:

- define the good packets,
- ensure the canonical source has nontrivial weighted mass on them,
- keep the residual \(R_X\) small.

This layer is purely scalar and positive-semidefinite.

### 2) Finite nondegeneracy layer
Once source mass survives, the next object is not yet a contradiction; it is a finite nondegeneracy certificate. That certificate has two forms:

\[
\mathcal H_{23}(A_p)\quad\text{for the graph/O2O3 block},
\]
and
\[
B_j \quad\text{for the D4-plane covariance}.
\]

So the second theorem is really:

\[
\text{on good packets, the graph block and the D4 plane are both nondegenerate.}
\]

This is where the draft currently has two separate-looking stories:

- Agent 2: thickened Schur survival for O2/O3,
- Agent 5: \(2\times 2\) PSD covariance survival for the D4 wall.

They are actually the same shape: finite matrix nondegeneracy after quotienting nuisance directions. The only difference is the matrix size and the observable being tested.

### 3) Quotient survival layer
This is the real hinge.

Every lower bound must survive the **same quotient** used by the forbidden upper. That quotient is the actual-space quotient
\[
Y_p/\mathcal K_p^Y,
\]
where \(\mathcal K_p^Y\) contains the actual-source nuisance directions but must not contain the primitive \(Y12\) carrier.

This is the layer where the current proof is most coherent if phrased as one theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{primitive }Y12\text{ survives in the quotient}
\iff
Y^{\tar}_{Y,p}\notin \mathcal K_p^Y.
}
\]

In the draft, this appears in several equivalent forms:

- labelled transition survival (\(\gamma_Y\)),
- retained-space sandwich (\(S_p\in \mathcal R_p^Y\), but \(d_{Y,p}\notin \mathcal R_p^Y+\mathcal T_p^Y\)),
- quotient-factorization (\(N_p^{D4}\subseteq\ker\Lambda_{Y,p}\)),
- Schur residual \(r_{Y,p}\neq 0\).

These should be merged into one statement:

> The primitive \(Y12\) carrier must descend to a nonzero class in the same quotient in which the D4 carrier acts and in which the forbidden upper is measured.

That is the key structural unification. Without this, the proof is only “visibility,” not contradiction. 

### 4) Atomic contradiction layer
The last layer is the same local square observable measured two ways:

- lower bound from the D4/Y12 carrier on good packets,
- upper bound from the forbidden singular-discard channel.

This should be phrased as a single atomic collision theorem:

\[
\sum_{p\in G}
|\Lambda_{Y,p}J_{\tr,p}(q''_{\can})|^2
\le Q^{-B}\mu(G),
\]
while
\[
\sum_{p\in G}
|H(p)K_{Y,p}\Gamma_p|^2
\ge Q^{-A}\mu(G),
\]
with a small error term.

Then contradiction follows if the same observable is controlled from both sides in the same quotient norm.

## What to call the unified objects

A coherent notation set would be:

\[
\mathscr S_p := \text{source packet observable},
\]
\[
\mathscr G_p := \text{graph/O2O3 matrix observable},
\]
\[
\mathscr Q_p := \text{quotient-survival observable},
\]
\[
\mathscr A_p := \text{atomic forbidden observable}.
\]

Then the proof is one pipeline:

\[
\mathscr S_p \Rightarrow \mathscr G_p \Rightarrow \mathscr Q_p \Rightarrow \mathscr A_p.
\]

Or, if you want the quotient to be the central object:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove one finite quotient-survival theorem}
}
\]
with three inputs:

- source mass survives,
- graph/D4 covariance survives,
- nuisance directions do not swallow the primitive \(Y12\) class.

## The clean theorem statement

A unified version of the whole architecture would read like this:

> On a polynomial-weight good packet set \(G\), the canonical source \(q''_{\can}\) has nontrivial \(L^2\) mass, the finite graph/O2O3 block has polynomial determinant mass, the primitive \(Y12\) carrier survives in the same quotient that kills actual-source nuisances, and the resulting D4/Y12 observable is simultaneously visible and forbidden-small. Therefore the same local square observable is bounded below and above by incompatible polynomial scales, giving contradiction.

That is the conceptual proof skeleton.

## What should be demoted or merged

Three things should be merged rather than treated separately:

1. **Gate–1 and extraction.**  
   Gate–1 is not a separate theorem after the reformulation. It is the source-mass part of the same packet-good-set theorem that later feeds extraction.

2. **Labelled transition and retained-space sandwich.**  
   These are the same quotient-survival issue in two coordinate systems.

3. **D4 visibility and forbidden upper.**  
   These are not separate endpoints. D4 visibility is only useful if it lives in the same quotient as the upper.

## A compact unified formulation

If you want the architecture in one line, it is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Choose good packets.}
\;\;
\text{Show canonical source, graph determinant, and D4 covariance all survive there.}
\;\;
\text{Project away actual-source nuisances without killing the primitive }Y12\text{ carrier.}
\;\;
\text{Use the same quotient to compare a local lower bound with a local atomic upper bound.}
}
\]

That is the coherent version of the current proof. The hidden common spine is finite PSD survival under quotienting. Everything else is an instantiation of that spine.

## Edit 1 — add the unified architecture section

**Where:** insert immediately after the opening material of `\label{sec:downstream-local-closure-package}` and before the first rank-two / D4 technical theorem in that section.

```latex
\section{Unified finite-survival architecture}
\label{sec:unified-finite-survival-architecture}

\begin{theorem}[Unified finite-survival theorem]
\label{thm:unified-finite-survival}
The proof is organized around four finite-survival statements:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Source survival:} \(\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})\) on a polynomial-weight good packet set.
\item \textbf{Graph survival:} \(\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}\) after \(R^C\)-normalization and full determinant survival.
\item \textbf{Quotient survival:} the primitive \(Y12\) carrier survives in the same quotient that removes actual-source nuisances.
\item \textbf{Atomic contradiction:} the singular-discard observable is Type-I local-square and is bounded above on the same quotient norm.
\end{enumerate}
If all four hold, the same observable is simultaneously bounded below and above by incompatible polynomial scales, giving the downstream contradiction.
\end{theorem}

\begin{equation}\label{eq:proof-architecture-diagram}
\begin{array}{c}
\boxed{\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})}
\\[3pt]
\Downarrow \quad \text{(packet-core micro-covering + EF completion)}
\\[3pt]
\boxed{\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}}
\\[3pt]
\Downarrow \quad \text{(\(R^C\)-normalized Riesz basis + thickened Schur survival)}
\\[3pt]
\boxed{Y12\text{-quotient survival}}
\\[3pt]
\Downarrow \quad \text{(retained-space sandwich + labelled transition)}
\\[3pt]
\boxed{\mathrm{AtomicY12Contradiction}}
\end{array}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Proof sketch}
\label{subsec:unified-proof-sketch}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Prove aggregate source observability for \(q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\) on a good packet set.
\item Prove finite graph nondegeneracy in the \(R^C\)-normalized augmented matrix and promote pure graph mass to full determinant survival.
\item Pass to the actual-source quotient: keep only EF-coherent retained directions, kill nuisances, and verify that the primitive \(Y12\) carrier remains nonzero in the quotient.
\item Compare the same quotient observable against the Type-I singular-discard upper and the \(Y12\)-wall lower bound; conclude contradiction when the lower and upper scales are separated.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Bookkeeping conventions}
\label{subsec:unified-bookkeeping}
The proof always uses the same observable in the same norm on both sides of each comparison. Source survival is measured before quotienting; contradiction is measured after quotienting by the actual-source nuisance space. D4 is only local visibility unless the forbidden channel \(\Lambda\) has been shown to be Type-I and quotient-compatible.
```

## Edit 2 — add the old-to-new framing section

**Where:** insert immediately before `\label{sec:no-go-and-audit-ledger}`.

```latex
\section{How the older framing maps to the new framing}
\label{sec:old-to-new-framing}

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{p{0.28\linewidth} p{0.30\linewidth} p{0.32\linewidth}}
\hline
Older framing & New framing & Status \\
\hline
Finite-row Gate--1 / O1a / O1b & \(\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})\) source survival & live, but only as scalar source observability \\
O2 / O3 incidence and exterior-pivot blocks & \(\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}\) thickened Schur survival & live \\
S1 / T1 transition/singular diagnostics & proof tools / anti-design inputs & historical tools, not live Gate--1 \\
Scalar \(I\)-coordinate D4 / derivative-wall D4 & \(\Lambda_{\tr,\sing,p}=(I-P_{\sing,p})T_{\tr\to\sing,p}P_{\tr,p}\) & dead or quarantined unless separately proved \\
Raw \(ad+bc\) row test & labelled \(Y12\) quotient survival via \(\gamma_Y\) & replaced \\
Optimized \(\Xi_N\) route & no-go registry & dead \\
One-parameter row mobility & no-go registry & dead \\
Full \(K_9\) or bust & stale; reduced to \(Y12\)-signature quotient plus \(\mathrm{EFCompletion}_{Y12}\) & historical only \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The current live chain is:
\[
\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})
\;\Rightarrow\;
\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}
\;\Rightarrow\;
Y12\text{-quotient survival}
\;\Rightarrow\;
\mathrm{AtomicY12Contradiction}.
\]
```

```latex
\end{remark}
```

The agent responses hide one strong unifier: every live module has been reduced to a **finite positivity / survival test under quotienting**. That is the real architecture now, not four separate proof attempts. turn22file16turn22file17

The cleanest hidden connection is between Agent 1, Agent 2, and Agent 5. Agent 1 shows that Gate–1 is really a **finite packet correlation matrix** problem: after normalizing by the reference Gram matrix, the source layer succeeds exactly when the normalized matrix is strictly diagonally dominant, equivalently when the off-diagonal correlations are small enough to give a polynomial spectral gap. 

Agent 2 shows the same structure on the graph side: once the Stack weight is Fejér–Riesz factored, the O2/O3 step becomes a **thickened-frequency Schur complement** problem. The true invariant is not merely support separation but the operator norm of the normalized overlap matrix \(K\). Support separation is only a sufficient special case; the actual finite criterion is whether the overlap graph has small enough degree/coherence that \(d\mu<1\) or, equivalently, \(\|K\|_{\mathrm{op}}<1\). turn23file0

Agent 5 is the same phenomenon one level downstream. The D4 extraction problem collapses to a \(2\times 2\) PSD covariance matrix \(B_j\), and the decisive quantity is \(\det(B_j)\), equivalently the weighted projective variance of the slope \(r_p=\Gamma_{G,2}(p)/\Gamma_G(p)\). The nice hidden point is that if the slope variance collapses, the wall is effectively static and the problem is no longer extraction; it has to be reclassified as a quotient-survival question. That is the bridge to the Y12 layer, not a separate issue. turn22file17

That brings out the second major hidden connection: Agent 3 and Agent 6 are really the same quotient test in two languages. Agent 3 reframes Y12 as a **labelled-transition / realization / Schur-residual** problem, with a primitive carrier scalar \(\gamma_Y\) and a quotient residual \(r_Y\). Agent 6 then packages the final contradiction as a compatibility defect: the D4 nuisance space must lie in the kernel of the Y12 observable, while the primitive \(Y12\) carrier must still survive the killed space. So the core condition is not “is the wall visible?” but “does the Y12 observable descend through the same quotient as the D4 nuisance directions, while leaving the primitive carrier nonzero?” turn22file11turn22file16

Agent 4 supplies the missing analytic bridge. Its hidden contribution is that the Y12 route does **not** follow from bare \(L^2\) completion; it needs a stronger EF norm that controls ninth-order jets through a Cauchy/sampling theorem. In other words, the route survives only if the discarded jet map is coercive with respect to the residual norm. That is why the retained-space Schur test and the analytic sampling theorem are the same bottleneck in two forms. turn22file11turn22file14

So the updated proof architecture maps cleanly as:

\[
\text{source correlation survival}
\;\to\;
\text{thickened Schur / determinant survival}
\;\to\;
\text{labelled }Y12\text{ quotient survival}
\;\to\;
\text{atomic contradiction}.
\]

A better way to say it is: each stage asks whether a finite observable survives after quotienting away nuisance directions, and whether the same observable is then forced small by the forbidden upper in the same norm. That is the shared spine across all the threads. turn22file11turn22file16

The main “goodies” hidden in the responses are these:
the source layer is now a Gram-matrix diagonal dominance problem;
the graph layer is a principal-angle / overlap-operator problem;
the D4 layer is a covariance-determinant / slope-variance problem;
the Y12 layer is a Schur-residual / quotient-membership problem.  
They are all the same proof pattern at different scales. turn22file13turn22file12turn22file11

The practical takeaway for the paper is that the old framing should be demoted to history, and the live framing should be written as a single unified finite-survival theorem with four instantiations: source, graph, quotient, contradiction.

Source, graph/O2O3, Y12, and extraction are not separate proof styles; they are four instances of the same “finite survival under projection” template. L6-L35 L969-L983 L4383-L4407 L5465-L5494

The sharpening opportunity is to stop stating these as separate audit notes and state one unified theorem with four reductions.

The cleanest version is:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Unified finite-survival theorem]
\label{thm:unified-finite-survival}
On the good packet set, the proof reduces to four finite survival statements:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Source survival:} the normalized packet Gram matrix
\[
M = G_{\ref}^{-1/2}G_{\branch}G_{\ref}^{-1/2}
\]
is strictly diagonally dominant up to the residual perturbation.

\item \emph{Graph/O2O3 survival:} after Fej\'er--Riesz thickening, the normalized overlap matrix
\[
K = G_{00}^{-1/2}G_{0S}G_{SS}^{-1/2}
\]
satisfies \(\|K\|_{\op}<1-Q^{-A}\).

\item \emph{Y12 quotient survival:} the projected operator
\[
\mathfrak T_p=(I-P_{U_p})T_{\tr\to\sing,p}J_{\tr,p},
\qquad
U_p=\operatorname{col}(B_p,N_p^{D4}),
\]
is coercive on the admissible residual class, and the primitive Y12 carrier survives the same quotient.

\item \emph{Extraction survival:} on each frozen cap,
\[
\det(B_j)\ge Q^{-A}(\operatorname{tr}B_j)^2
\]
or else the wall is static and is handed to the Y12 quotient module.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}
```

This is the right umbrella statement because the agent responses show that each stage has already been reduced to a finite matrix test: source to a Gram matrix, graph/O2O3 to an overlap operator, Y12 to a projected quotient operator, and extraction to a \(2\times2\) covariance matrix. L6-L35 L975-L983 L4385-L4407 L5637-L5728

The strongest hidden structural link is between the Y12 layer and the graph-space layer. The “finite-codimension graph space” is not a separate missing theorem; it is exactly the decomposition of the admissible residual space into a finite low block plus a tail, with the D4 transversality matrix as the low-block defect matrix. That is already implicit in the draft’s retained/discard split and singular-discard upper. L3108-L3145

So I would insert this lemma, because it sharpens the paper more than the longer prose does:

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Finite-codimension Y12 graph/coercivity lemma]
\label{lem:finite-codim-y12-graph}
Let \(U_p=\operatorname{col}(B_p,N_p^{D4})\), and set
\[
\mathfrak T_p=(I-P_{\sing,p})T_{\tr\to\sing,p}J_{\tr,p}.
\]
Assume the admissible residual class \(\mathcal R_X\) splits as
\[
\mathcal R_X=\mathcal R_{X,\low,p}\oplus \mathcal R_{X,\tail,p},
\qquad
\dim \mathcal R_{X,\low,p}<\infty,
\]
where the low block is controlled by the finite defect matrix
\[
D_p=\begin{bmatrix}\mathfrak T_p e_{1,p} & \cdots & \mathfrak T_p e_{r,p}\end{bmatrix}
\]
for a basis \(\{e_{1,p},\dots,e_{r,p}\}\) of \(\mathcal R_{X,\low,p}\), and the tail is controlled by the singular-discard upper.
If
\[
\sigma_{\min}(D_p)\ge Q^{-C}
\quad\text{and}\quad
U_p\subseteq \ker \Lambda_{Y,p},
\]
then \(\mathfrak T_p\) is coercive up to the tail norm, and the Y12 carrier survives as a genuine quotient observable.
\end{lemma}
```

Why this sharpens the theorem: it packages the exact logic the agents kept rediscovering. The draft already has the ingredients for this lemma, but scattered across the retained space, the singular-discard upper, the Y12 quotient, and the D4 transversality matrix. The hidden connection is that these are all the same low-mode/tail split written in different labels. L3129-L3151 L5637-L5728

The quotient-descent piece should be sharpened too. The current lemma is good, but it should explicitly state the factorization and the Schur residual in one place. That is the exact finite form of the bridge:

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Y12 quotient descent and primitive survival]
\label{lem:Y12-quotient-descent}
Assume
\[
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12),p}T_{\tr\to\sing,p}\mathcal N_p^{D4}\subseteq \mathcal K_p^Y,
\qquad
\mathcal K_p^Y=\operatorname{im}
\begin{bmatrix}
R_{B_2,p}&R_{P,p}&R_{D,p}&A_{\alpha,p}&A_{7,p}&A_{<7,p}&A_{II,p}&A_{E_2,p}
\end{bmatrix}.
\]
Then the forbidden observable factors through the D4 quotient, and the primitive Y12 target satisfies
\[
r_{Y,p}
=
(I-P_{\mathcal K_p^Y}^{\mathrm{bd}})Y_{Y,p}^{\tar},
\]
so
\[
r_{Y,p}=0 \iff Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}\in \mathcal K_p^Y.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\operatorname{rank}
\begin{bmatrix}
\mathcal K_p^Y & \Pi_{\Sigma(Y12),p}T_{\tr\to\sing,p}\mathcal N_p^{D4}
\end{bmatrix}
=
\operatorname{rank}(\mathcal K_p^Y),
\]
and
\[
\operatorname{rank}
\begin{bmatrix}
\mathcal K_p^Y & Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}
\end{bmatrix}
=
\operatorname{rank}(\mathcal K_p^Y)+1
\]
is the precise primitive-survival condition.
\end{lemma}
```

That theorem is sharper than the current prose because it makes the two conditions explicit and separate: descent of the nuisance image, and survival of the primitive carrier. It also matches the exact rank language the agents converged to. L5465-L5494 L5637-L5728

The extraction module should also be sharpened by folding the “moving wall” and “static line” cases into one statement. Right now the agents already reduced it to a \(2\times2\) PSD determinant and a quotient-angle fallback; that should be stated as a single lemma:

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Extraction covariance dichotomy]
\label{lem:extraction-covariance-dichotomy}
On each frozen cap \(C_j\), let
\[
B_j=\sum_{p\in C_j} w_p\,\Gamma_p\Gamma_p^\ast,
\qquad
w_p=\rho_p\frac{E_{1,p}H_p}{N_p}.
\]
Then either
\[
\det(B_j)\ge Q^{-A}(\operatorname{tr}B_j)^2,
\]
equivalently the projective slope variance is \(\ge Q^{-A}\), or else \(B_j\) is nearly rank one and the frozen line must be tested in the Y12 quotient by the Schur complement
\[
|(I-P_{\mathcal K_j^Y})u_j|^2.
\]
\end{lemma}
```

This is the right sharpened version because it removes the repeated rephrasing of the same covariance test and makes the “static wall \(\to\) quotient module” handoff explicit. L4383-L4407

The source layer likewise should be sharpened from “Gram matrix diagonal dominance” to “oscillatory kernel decay implies blockwise invertibility.” The late agent responses show the source proof has already been compressed to a Fourier-kernel estimate plus resonant block conditioning, so that should appear as a lemma rather than prose:

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Oscillatory packet kernel decay]
\label{lem:packet-oscillatory-kernel-decay}
Let \(\psi_p(t)=a_p(t)e^{i\omega_p t}\) and \(\psi_q(t)=a_q(t)e^{i\omega_q t}\), with \(a_p,a_q\) supported on packet cores and with polynomial derivative bounds. Then
\[
\langle \psi_p,\psi_q\rangle_{W_{\branch}}
=
\widehat{F_{pq}}(\omega_p-\omega_q),
\]
and the cross terms satisfy polynomial Fourier decay. Consequently, the source Gram matrix is diagonally dominant once the resonant blocks are uniformly invertible.
\end{lemma}
```

This lemma is the analytic form of the same finite matrix test and is the right source-side sharpening. L6-L35

So the hidden connections are:

the source and O2/O3 layers are both overlap-operator problems,
the Y12 and graph-space layers are both projected-operator / defect-matrix problems,
and the extraction layer is the same story in \(2\times2\) covariance form. The theorem sharpenings should therefore compress the whole draft into one unified finite-survival theorem with four explicitly stated lemmas underneath it. L969-L983 L3129-L3151 L4385-L4407 L5637-L5728

## Edit 1 — insert one unified finite-survival theorem at the top of the downstream package

**Where:** `sec:downstream-local-closure-package`, immediately after `\label{thm:rank-two-closure-spine}` and before `\label{def:rank-two-covariant-septic-row}`.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Unified finite-survival theorem]
\label{thm:unified-finite-survival}
On the good packet set, the proof reduces to four finite survival statements:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Source survival:} the normalized packet Gram matrix
\[
M=G_{\ref}^{-1/2}G_{\branch}G_{\ref}^{-1/2}
\]
is strictly diagonally dominant up to the residual perturbation.

\item \textbf{Graph/O2O3 survival:} after Fej\'er--Riesz thickening, the normalized overlap matrix
\[
K=G_{00}^{-1/2}G_{0S}G_{SS}^{-1/2}
\]
satisfies \(\|K\|_{\op}<1-Q^{-A}\).

\item \textbf{Y12 quotient survival:} the projected operator
\[
\mathfrak T_p=(I-P_{\sing,p})T_{\tr\to\sing,p}J_{\tr,p}
\]
is coercive on the admissible residual class, and the primitive \(Y12\) carrier survives the quotient \(\mathcal K_p^Y\).

\item \textbf{Extraction survival:} on each frozen cap,
\[
\det(B_j)\ge Q^{-A}(\operatorname{tr}B_j)^2
\]
or else the wall is static and is handed to the Y12 quotient module.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{equation}\label{eq:proof-architecture-diagram}
\begin{array}{c}
\boxed{\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})}
\\[3pt]
\Downarrow \quad \text{(packet correlation / EF completion)}
\\[3pt]
\boxed{\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}}
\\[3pt]
\Downarrow \quad \text{(thickened Schur / overlap control)}
\\[3pt]
\boxed{Y12\text{-quotient survival}}
\\[3pt]
\Downarrow \quad \text{(retained-space / Schur residual)}
\\[3pt]
\boxed{\mathrm{AtomicY12Contradiction}}
\end{array}
\end{equation}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
The source layer is a finite packet-correlation matrix; the O2/O3 layer is a thickened overlap matrix; the Y12 layer is a projected quotient operator with a Schur residual; the extraction layer is a \(2\times2\) covariance test.  Each step is a finite positivity / survival statement under quotienting away nuisance directions.
\end{proof}
```

## Edit 2 — make the Y12 graph/coercivity theorem explicit in the downstream closure section

**Where:** `sec:downstream-local-closure-package`, immediately after `\label{def:singular-retained-space-and-discard-lambda}`.

```latex
\begin{definition}[Combined nuisance block and projected transition operator]
\label{def:combined-nuisance-block-y12}
For each packet \(p\), define the combined Y12 nuisance block
\[
U_p := \operatorname{span}\!\bigl(T_{\par}^{(\alpha)},\,T_7,\,T_{<7},\,II_{\arith,9},\,T_{E_2}\bigr),
\]
with the understanding that \(T_{E_2}\) is included only when \(E_2\) is admitted in the current quotient layer.

Define the projected transition operator
\[
\mathfrak T_p := (I-P_{\sing,p})\,T_{\tr\to\sing,p}\,J_{\tr,p}.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Finite-codimension Y12 graph/coercivity lemma]
\label{lem:finite-codim-y12-graph}
Assume that the Y12 quotient annihilates the combined nuisance block,
\[
U_p \subseteq \ker \Lambda_{Y,p},
\]
and that the admissible residual class \(\mathcal R_X\) splits as a finite-codimension graph space
\[
\mathcal R_X = \mathcal R_{X,\low,p}\oplus \mathcal R_{X,\tail,p},
\qquad
\dim \mathcal R_{X,\low,p}<\infty.
\]
Let \(\{e_{1,p},\dots,e_{r,p}\}\) be a basis of \(\mathcal R_{X,\low,p}\), and define the defect matrix
\[
D_p := \begin{bmatrix}
\mathfrak T_p e_{1,p} & \cdots & \mathfrak T_p e_{r,p}
\end{bmatrix}.
\]
If
\[
\sigma_{\min}(D_p)\ge Q^{-C}
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\sum_p \|\mathfrak T_p(R_X)\|^2 \le Q^{-B}\mu(\mathcal C),
\]
then \(\mathfrak T_p\) is coercive on \(\mathcal R_X\) up to the tail norm, and the Y12 discarded observable survives on a polynomial-weight good set.
\end{lemma}

\begin{remark}[Defect matrix and D4 transversality]
\label{rem:defect-matrix-d4-transversality}
The finite defect matrix \(D_p\) is the low-mode representation of the same discarded operator encoded by
\[
K_{\Dfour,p}
=
(I-P_{\sing,p})T_{\tr\to\sing,p}E_{\car,p}^{\tr}L_{\clean,p}^{\tr}.
\]
Thus the coercivity of \(\mathfrak T_p\) on the low block and the rank condition for \(K_{\Dfour,p}\) are the same finite test in two coordinate systems.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Graph-space no-go]
\label{rem:graph-space-no-go}
If \(U_p\not\subseteq\ker\Lambda_{Y,p}\), or if \(\mathcal R_X\) fails to admit a finite-codimension graph decomposition with tail norm \(\|\cdot\|_{\EF}\), then the Y12 discarded observable is not coercive and the downstream atomic contradiction cannot be derived in the current norm.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 3 — add the exact Y12 quotient descent lemma in the no-go/audit ledger

**Where:** `sec:no-go-and-audit-ledger`, immediately after `\begin{remark}[Unified live/dead dictionary]` and before `rem:terminal-conditional-dependency-ledger`.

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Y12 quotient descent and primitive survival]
\label{lem:Y12-quotient-descent}
For each packet \(p\), define
\[
\mathcal K_p^Y
:=
\operatorname{im}
\begin{bmatrix}
R_{B_2,p}&R_{P,p}&R_{D,p}&A_{\alpha,p}&A_{7,p}&A_{<7,p}&A_{II,p}&A_{E_2,p}
\end{bmatrix},
\qquad
q_p^Y:=I-P_{\mathcal K_p^Y}^{\mathrm{bd}},
\]
and let
\[
\Lambda_{Y,p}
:=
q_p^Y\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12),p}T_{\tr\to\sing,p}P_{\tr,p}.
\]
Assume the D4 nuisance image is killed by the same quotient:
\[
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12),p}T_{\tr\to\sing,p}\mathcal N_p^{D4}
\subseteq
\mathcal K_p^Y.
\]
Then \(\Lambda_{Y,p}\) factors through the D4 quotient \(V_p/N_p^{D4}\). Moreover, if
\[
Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}
:=
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12),p}T_{\tr\to\sing,p}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]^{\tr},
\]
then the Schur residual
\[
r_{Y,p}
:=
(I-P_{\mathcal K_p^Y}^{\mathrm{bd}})Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}
\]
vanishes if and only if \(Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}\in \mathcal K_p^Y\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
If \(v-v'\in N_p^{D4}\), then by hypothesis
\[
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12),p}T_{\tr\to\sing,p}(v-v')\in \mathcal K_p^Y,
\]
hence
\[
q_p^Y\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12),p}T_{\tr\to\sing,p}(v-v')=0.
\]
Therefore \(\Lambda_{Y,p}(v)=\Lambda_{Y,p}(v')\), so \(\Lambda_{Y,p}\) is constant on cosets of \(N_p^{D4}\) and descends to a unique induced map on \(V_p/N_p^{D4}\).

For the residual statement, let \(A_p\) be any matrix whose columns span \(\mathcal K_p^Y\). Then
\[
r_{Y,p}=(I-P_{\mathcal K_p^Y}^{\mathrm{bd}})Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}
\]
and
\[
\|r_{Y,p}\|^2
=
\|Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}\|^2
-
(Y_{Y,p}^{\tar})^*A_p(A_p^*A_p)^\dagger A_p^*Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}.
\]
Hence \(r_{Y,p}=0\) precisely when \(Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}\in \mathcal K_p^Y\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Rank form]
\label{cor:Y12-quotient-rank}
With the notation of Lemma~\ref{lem:Y12-quotient-descent},
\[
\operatorname{rank}
\begin{bmatrix}
\mathcal K_p^Y & \Pi_{\Sigma(Y12),p}T_{\tr\to\sing,p}\mathcal N_p^{D4}
\end{bmatrix}
=
\operatorname{rank}(\mathcal K_p^Y)
\]
if and only if the \(Y12\) observable descends through the D4 quotient, and
\[
\operatorname{rank}
\begin{bmatrix}
\mathcal K_p^Y & Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}
\end{bmatrix}
=
\operatorname{rank}(\mathcal K_p^Y)+1
\]
if and only if the primitive \(Y12\) carrier survives the quotient.
\end{corollary}

\noindent
In particular, the current \(D4\to Y12\) route reduces to the two finite checks
\[
\Pi_{\Sigma(Y12)}T_{\tr\to\sing}\mathcal N_p^{D4}\subseteq \mathcal K_p^Y
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
Y_{Y,p}^{\tar}\notin \mathcal K_p^Y.
\]
```

## Edit 4 — replace the source layer with the oscillatory kernel / resonant block theorem

**Where:** `subsec:branch-complete-local-l2-gate-one` (or the source-layer subsection you currently use for Gate–1), replacing the present “diagonal dominance / packet correlation” prose.

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Oscillatory packet kernel decay]
\label{lem:packet-oscillatory-kernel-decay}
Let \(\psi_p(t)=a_p(t)e^{i\omega_p t}\) and \(\psi_q(t)=a_q(t)e^{i\omega_q t}\), with \(a_p,a_q\in C^N\) supported on packet cores and satisfying
\[
\|\partial_t^j a_p\|_\infty+\|\partial_t^j a_q\|_\infty \le Q^{Cj}
\qquad (0\le j\le N).
\]
Then
\[
\langle \psi_p,\psi_q\rangle_{W_{\branch}}
=\widehat{F_{pq}}(\omega_p-\omega_q),
\qquad
F_{pq}(t)=a_p(t)\overline{a_q(t)}W_{\branch}(t),
\]
and hence
\[
|\langle \psi_p,\psi_q\rangle_{W_{\branch}}|
\le C_N Q^{C_N}(1+|\omega_p-\omega_q|)^{-N}.
\]
In particular, if \(|\omega_p-\omega_q|\ge Q^{-\delta}\) outside resonant blocks, then the off-diagonal correlation is \(Q^{-A}\)-small for \(N\) large enough.
\end{lemma}

\begin{remark}[Resonant block conditioning]
\label{rem:source-resonant-block-conditioning}
If \(|\omega_p-\omega_q|<Q^{-\delta}\), the pair must be handled inside a resonant block \(B\). It is enough to prove
\[
G_B\ge Q^{-A}G_{B,\ref}
\]
for every resonant block.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 5 — sharpen the O2/O3 subsection to the normalized overlap / Schur criterion

**Where:** `subsec:finite-o2o3-23`, immediately after `lem:riesz-normalized-determinant-controls-H23`.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Thickened overlap Schur criterion]
\label{thm:thickened-o2o3-schur}
Let
\[
K:=G_{00}^{-1/2}G_{0S}G_{SS}^{-1/2}
\]
after Fej\'er--Riesz thickening of the Stack weight. Then
\[
G_{00}-G_{0S}G_{SS}^{\dagger}G_{S0}\ge Q^{-A}G_{00}
\]
if and only if
\[
\|K\|_{\op}\le 1-Q^{-A}.
\]
A sufficient finite criterion is
\[
\Bigl(\max_i\sum_j |K_{ij}|\Bigr)\Bigl(\max_j\sum_i |K_{ij}|\Bigr)<(1-Q^{-A})^2.
\]
Equivalently, if \(K\) is viewed as a weighted bipartite overlap graph, then a coherence bound \(d\mu<1-Q^{-A}\) suffices.
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[O2/O3 failure modes]
\label{rem:o2o3-thickened-overlap-failure}
The only local failure mode at this stage is thickened overlap too coherent. The upstream prerequisites are \(R^C\)-normalization and genuine-pole/divided-difference visibility; if either fails, the overlap matrix is not in the correct finite regime.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 6 — sharpen the extraction layer to the \(2\times2\) covariance dichotomy

**Where:** in the downstream package, near the D4 / moving-wall extraction discussion (the place where the current draft discusses the cap-by-cap row energy or moving wall), or immediately after the rank-selector / D4-bridge discussion.

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Extraction covariance dichotomy]
\label{lem:extraction-covariance-dichotomy}
On each frozen cap \(C_j\), let
\[
B_j=\sum_{p\in C_j} w_p\,\Gamma_p\Gamma_p^\ast,
\qquad
w_p=\rho_p\frac{E_{1,p}H_p}{N_p},
\qquad
\Gamma_p=\binom{\Gamma_G(p)}{\Gamma_{G,2}(p)}.
\]
Then either
\[
\det(B_j)\ge Q^{-A}(\operatorname{tr}B_j)^2,
\]
equivalently
\[
\sum_{p\in C_j}\lambda_p|r_p-\bar r_j|^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]
where \(r_p=\Gamma_{G,2}(p)/\Gamma_G(p)\) on the chart \(|\Gamma_G|\ge \tfrac12|\Gamma|\), or else \(B_j\) is nearly rank one and the wall is effectively static.
In the static-line case, one must hand the cap to the Y12 quotient test:
\[
\eta_j:=|(I-P_{\mathcal K_j^Y})u_j|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]
\end{lemma}
```

## Exact places to change

### 1. `lem:clean-triangular-d4-carrier-matrix`
This is the main place that should be rewritten.

**Section / environment:**  
`\begin{lemma}[Clean triangular D4 carrier matrix]`  
` \label{lem:clean-triangular-d4-carrier-matrix}`

**Current lines to replace:** roughly `38484–38624`, especially:
- the clean order-nine carrier display at `38552–38560`
- the definition of \(\beta_9(g,h,u)\) at `38571–38574`
- the matrix display at `38587–38602`
- the determinant display at `38607–38618`

**Rewrite it so the row-normalized coefficient is explicit:**
```latex
\begin{lemma}[Clean triangular D4 carrier matrix]
\label{lem:clean-triangular-d4-carrier-matrix}
In the D4 finite carrier calculation, write the centered Gram diagonal scalars as
\[
g_{\rm Gr}:=\frac{q_0}{\pi},
\qquad
h_{\rm Gr}:=
\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16u\right),
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]
Let \(\kappa=\omega_Y(e_7)\), and define the row-normal coefficient
\[
\beta_9^{\tri}(g,h,u):=\beta_9(g,h,u)-\kappa\,c_7(g,h).
\]
Then
\[
g_{\rm Gr}-h_{\rm Gr}
=
-\frac{\Gamma_G}{6\pi}.
\]
In these triangular coordinates, the clean order-nine carrier coordinate is
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
H\left(
\beta_9^{\tri}(g,h,u)\Gamma_G
+
\alpha_9(g,h)\Gamma_{G,2}
\right)I,
\]
where
\[
\alpha_9(g,h)
=
\frac{1}
{64\pi^2\sqrt{gh}\,h^{3/2}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)}
\]
and
\[
\beta_9^{\tri}(g,h,u)
=
-\frac{\rho_9(g,h,u)}
{2\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)}
-\kappa\,c_7(g,h).
\]
In particular, on \(g=h\),
\[
\alpha_9(g,g)=\frac1{128\pi^2g^3},
\]
recovering the clean wall formula
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_9^{(1,2)}
=
\frac{H\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
\]

Thus, in the clean carrier coordinates,
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
B_7\\
B_9
\end{pmatrix}
=
H
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
\beta_9^{\tri}&\alpha_9
\end{pmatrix}
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
The same-scale \(\beta_9^{\tri}\Gamma_G\) term belongs to the effective leading matrix, not a residual.  Moreover
\[
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
\beta_9^{\tri}&\alpha_9
\end{pmatrix}
=
c_7\alpha_9
=
-\frac{1}
{1536\pi^4
g^{3/2}h^3(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)^3}.
\]
Consequently this clean D4 carrier matrix is polynomially invertible on every
Gram-good patch on which
\[
Q^{-C}\le g_{\rm Gr},h_{\rm Gr}\le Q^C.
\]
\end{lemma}
```

This is the place where the raw \(\beta_9\) should be removed in favor of \(\beta_9^{\tri}\) if the section is meant to be row-normal.

_Thought for 22s_

The draft now reduces the proof to a short finite checklist. The remaining work is exactly these five steps, in this order of dependency:

1. **Close Gate–1 / source survival in `subsec:branch-complete-local-l2-gate-one`.**  
   Prove the packet cross-term decay lemma `lem:packet-oscillatory-kernel-decay`, then show every resonant packet block is uniformly invertible. Equivalently, prove the normalized source Gram matrix  
   \[
   M=G_{\ref}^{-1/2}G_{\branch}G_{\ref}^{-1/2}
   \]
   is diagonally dominant after the residual perturbation. This is the remaining source-layer obstruction. 

2. **Close `subsec:finite-o2o3-23` by a thickened Schur bound.**  
   After Fejér–Riesz thickening, prove
   \[
   K=G_{00}^{-1/2}G_{0S}G_{SS}^{-1/2}
   \qquad\text{satisfies}\qquad
   \|K\|_{\op}<1-Q^{-A}.
   \]
   In practice this means one of:
   \[
   d\mu<1-Q^{-A},\qquad \mu\sqrt{d_0d_1}<1-Q^{-A},
   \]
   or a direct Schur-complement lower bound. The only local failure mode left there is thickened overlap too coherent. turn40file2turn40file3turn40file7turn40file8turn40file9

3. **Prove the Y12 quotient descent in `sec:downstream-local-closure-package`.**  
   For the combined nuisance block
   \[
   U_p=\operatorname{col}(T_{\par}^{(\alpha)},T_7,T_{<7},II_{\arith,9},T_{E_2}),
   \]
   prove
   \[
   U_p\subseteq\ker\Lambda_{Y,p},
   \]
   so the forbidden observable descends through the D4 quotient. Then prove the finite-codimension graph/coercivity lemma: the admissible residual class splits into low modes plus tail, the defect matrix \(D_p\) has
   \[
   \sigma_{\min}(D_p)\ge Q^{-C},
   \]
   and the tail is controlled by the singular-discard upper. This is the real bridge theorem for the Y12 layer. turn40file6

4. **Finish the extraction layer with the covariance dichotomy.**  
   On each frozen cap \(C_j\), prove either
   \[
   \det(B_j)\ge Q^{-A}(\operatorname{tr}B_j)^2
   \]
   or else the wall is static and the frozen line survives the Y12 quotient:
   \[
   |(I-P_{\mathcal K_j^Y})u_j|\ge Q^{-A}.
   \]
   The draft has already reduced this to the projective slope variance
   \[
   \mathrm{Var}_j(r)=\sum_{p\in C_j}\lambda_p|r_p-\bar r_j|^2.
   \]
   So the remaining extraction task is just: show variance survives, or hand the static line to the quotient module. 

5. **Turn the Y12 quotient survival into the final contradiction.**  
   Once 1–4 hold, the last step is formal:
   \[
   (I-P_{U_p})Y_{\tar,p}\neq 0
   \quad\text{with polynomial margin,}
   \]
   and the Type-I upper for the singular-discard map is in the same quotient norm. That gives the final atomic contradiction. This is exactly the point of `lem:Y12-quotient-descent`, `cor:Y12-quotient-rank`, and `lem:projected-y12-coercivity`. turn40file6

So, in one line: **prove source diagonal dominance, prove thickened Schur subcriticality, prove Y12 quotient descent plus graph-space coercivity, prove covariance spread or static-line quotient survival, then compare the same quotient norm upper and lower.** Everything else in the draft is now bookkeeping.

_Thought for 5s_

We added a unified finite-survival architecture and pushed the draft into a much cleaner proof shape. The main new top-level theorem is the unified finite-survival theorem, with the proof diagram showing the pipeline
\[
\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can}) \to \mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23} \to Y12\text{-quotient survival} \to \mathrm{AtomicY12Contradiction}.
\]
That became the organizing spine of the downstream section. turn45file1

We also made the Y12 layer explicit in finite-linear-algebra terms. That includes the combined nuisance block \(U_p\), the projected operator \(\mathfrak T_p=(I-P_{\sing,p})T_{\tr\to\sing,p}J_{\tr,p}\), the finite-codimension graph/coercivity lemma, and the quotient-descent lemma showing how the forbidden observable factors through the D4 quotient and how the primitive Y12 carrier is tested by a Schur residual / rank condition. turn45file4

On the source side, we added the packet-correlation / oscillatory-kernel reduction: Gate–1 is now framed as a normalized packet Gram matrix problem, with oscillatory decay for off-diagonal packet terms and resonant block conditioning as the remaining finite input. 

On the O2/O3 side, we added the thickened Schur criterion: after Fejér–Riesz thickening, the problem is reduced to the normalized overlap matrix \(K\), with a concrete subcriticality test \(\|K\|_{\op}<1-Q^{-A}\) and row/column-sum coherence bounds. turn45file9

On the extraction side, we added the \(2\times2\) covariance dichotomy: on each frozen cap, either
\[
\det(B_j)\ge Q^{-A}(\operatorname{tr}B_j)^2
\]
or the wall is effectively static and the cap is handed to the Y12 quotient module. That was sharpened into a projective slope-variance test. turn45file12

We also consolidated the historical material into a single register. The old O1/O2/O3, scalar \(I\)-coordinate D4, derivative-wall D4, optimized \(\Xi_N\), and one-parameter row-mobility routes are now meant to live in a terse historical/no-go remark rather than being spread through the active proof text. 

The draft is therefore much more coherent now: the live sections are theorem-driven, and the older branches are being demoted to a compact archive. The only lingering cleanup is the one historical pre-triangular block that still uses raw \(\beta_9\) instead of \(\beta_9^{\tri}\). turn45file13
